class="mw-indicators">\n\t\t</div>\n\n\t\t\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"><div id="mw-content-subtitle"></div></div>\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t\n\t\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Viewing cetaceans in their habitats</div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ballenafranca%2Balvina.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Ballenafranca%2Balvina.jpg/220px-Ballenafranca%2Balvina.jpg" peninsula</a></figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Whale_watching_boats.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Humpback_whales_in_Monterey_Bay.jpg/330px-Humpback_whales_in_Monterey_Bay.jpg 1.5x, Bay, 2013</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach,_CA.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach%2C_CA.jpg/220px-Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach%2C_CA.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach%2C_CA.jpg/330px-Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach%2C_CA.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach%2C_CA.jpg/440px-Humpback_Whale_off_Avila_Beach%2C_CA.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1735" data-file-height="1157" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">Humpback whale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brown_pelican" title="Brown pelican">brown pelicans</a> off <a href="/wiki/Avila_Beach,_California" title="Avila Beach, California">Avila Beach, California</a> </figcaption></figure>\n<p><b>Whale watching</b> is the practice of observing <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cetacean" class="mw-redirect" title="Cetacean">cetaceans</a>) in their natural habitat. Whale watching is mostly a recreational activity (cf. <a href="/wiki/Birdwatching" title="Birdwatching">birdwatching</a>), but it can also serve scientific and/or educational purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A study prepared for <a href="/wiki/International_Fund_for_Animal_Welfare" title="International Fund for Animal Welfare">International Fund for Animal Welfare</a> in 2009 estimated that 13 million people went whale watching globally in 2008. Whale watching generates $2.1 billion per annum in tourism revenue worldwide, employing around 13,000 workers.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor2009_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor2009-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The size and rapid growth of the industry has led to complex and continuing debates with the <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> industry about the best use of whales as a <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resource</a>.\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-3"><meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" /></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Organized whale watching started in the United States, when the <a href="/wiki/Cabrillo_National_Monument" title="Cabrillo National Monument">Cabrillo National Monument</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego</a> was declared a public venue for observing the migration of <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">gray whales</a>; the spectacle attracted 10,000 visitors in its first year, 1950.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1955 the first water-based whale watching commenced in the same area, charging customers $1 per trip to view the whales at closer quarters.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The industry spread throughout the western coast of the United States over the following decade.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1971 the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Zoological_Society&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Montreal Zoological Society (page does not exist)">Montreal Zoological Society</a> commenced the first commercial whale watching activity on the eastern side of North America, offering trips in the <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a> to view <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beluga_whale" title="Beluga whale">beluga whales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> By the mid-1970s, live captures for aquaria had reduced the orca populations in the coastal waters of British Columbia and Washington, particularly the <a href="/wiki/Southern_resident_orcas" title="Southern resident orcas">southern resident orca</a> population. According to their scientific chroniclers, in the 1980s commercial whale watching started becoming an alternative means of viewing and appreciating orcas.<sup id="cite_ref-Ford,_Ellis_&amp;_Balcomb,_2000_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ford,_Ellis_&amp;_Balcomb,_2000-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1984, <a href="/wiki/Erich_Hoyt" title="Erich Hoyt">Erich Hoyt</a>, who had spent much time amongst the <a href="/wiki/Orca" title="Orca">orcas</a> of British Columbia, published the first comprehensive book on whale watching, <i>The Whale Watcher\'s Handbook</i>, which <a href="/wiki/Mark_Carwardine" title="Mark Carwardine">Mark Carwardine</a> called his number one "natural classic" book in <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_Wildlife" title="BBC Wildlife">BBC Wildlife</a></i> magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>By 1985 more visitors watched whales from <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> than California. The rapid growth in this area has been attributed to the relatively dense population of <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Cetacean_surfacing_behaviour" title="Cetacean surfacing behaviour">acrobatic behavior</a> such as breaching (jumping out of the water) and tail-slapping thrilled observers, and the close proximity of whale populations to the large cities there.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Whale watching tourism has grown substantially since the mid-1980s. The first worldwide survey of whale watching was conducted by Hoyt for the <a href="/wiki/Whale_and_Dolphin_Conservation_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Whale and Dolphin Conservation Society">Whale and Dolphin Conservation Society</a> (WDCS) in 1992. It was updated in 1995 and submitted by the UK government to the <a href="/wiki/International_Whaling_Commission" title="International Whaling Commission">International Whaling Commission</a> (IWC) meetings as a demonstration of the value of living whales.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 1999, the <a href="/wiki/International_Fund_for_Animal_Welfare" title="International Fund for Animal Welfare">International Fund for Animal Welfare</a> (IFAW) asked Hoyt for another expansion, which was published in 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2009 the survey was completed by a team of economists and this report estimated that in 2008, 13 million people went whale watching, up from 9 million ten years earlier. Commercial whale watching operations were found in 119 countries. Direct revenue of whale watching trips was estimated at US$872.7 million and indirect revenue of $2,113.1 million was spent by whale watchers in tourism-related businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor2009_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor2009-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Whale watching is of particular importance to developing countries. Coastal communities have started to profit directly from the whales\' presence, significantly adding to popular support for the protection of these animals from commercial whaling and other threats such as bycatch and ship strikes using the tool of <a href="/wiki/Marine_protected_areas" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine protected areas">marine protected areas</a> and sanctuaries. In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/Humane_Society_International" title="Humane Society International">Humane Society International</a> sponsored a series of workshops to introduce whale watching to coastal Peru and commissioned Hoyt to write a blueprint for high quality, sustainable whale watching.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2012_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2012-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This manual, later translated into Spanish, French, Indonesian, Japanese, Chinese and Dutch, with co-sponsorship from WDCS, IFAW and Global Ocean was updated in English in 2012 in ebook form.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2012_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2012-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Conservation">Conservation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Conservation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Whale-watching-australia.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Whale-watching-australia.jpg/220px-Whale-watching-australia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f0/Whale-watching-australia.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="314" data-file-height="209" /></a><figcaption>Whale watching operator giving a talk about whales and their conservation</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_(49040807441).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_%2849040807441%29.jpg/220px-MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_%2849040807441%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_%2849040807441%29.jpg/330px-MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_%2849040807441%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_%2849040807441%29.jpg/440px-MBNMS_kayaker_too_close_to_humpback_whale_%2849040807441%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="2048" /></a><figcaption>An example of being too close</figcaption></figure>\n<p>The rapid growth of the number of whale watching trips and the size of vessel used to watch whales may affect whale behavior, migratory patterns and breeding cycles. There is now strong evidence that whale watching can significantly affect the biology and ecology of whales and dolphins.\n</p><p>Environmental campaigners, concerned by what they consider the "quick-buck" mentality of some boat owners, continue to strongly urge all whale watcher operators to contribute to local regulations governing whale watching (no international standard set of regulations exist because of the huge variety of species and populations). Common rules include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Minimize speed/"No wake" speed</li>\n<li>Avoid sudden turns</li>\n<li>Minimize noise</li>\n<li>Do not pursue, encircle or come in between whales</li>\n<li>Approach animals from angles where they will not be taken by surprise</li>\n<li>Consider cumulative impact \xe2\x80\x93 minimize number of boats at any one time/per day</li>\n<li>Do not coerce dolphins into bow-riding.</li>\n<li>Do not allow <a href="/wiki/Swimming_with_dolphins" title="Swimming with dolphins">swimming with dolphins</a>. (This last rule is more contentious and is often disregarded in, for example, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>.) In New Zealand, the rules adopted under the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Mammals_Protection_Act" title="Marine Mammals Protection Act">Marine Mammals Protection Act</a> specifically allow swimming with dolphins and seals but not with juvenile dolphins or a pod of dolphins that includes juvenile dolphins.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>(Source: <a href="/wiki/Whale_and_Dolphin_Conservation" title="Whale and Dolphin Conservation">WDCS</a>)\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Avistamiento.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Avistamiento.JPG/220px-Avistamiento.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="184" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Avistamiento.JPG/330px-Avistamiento.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Avistamiento.JPG/440px-Avistamiento.JPG 2x" data-file-width="547" data-file-height="457" /></a><figcaption>Whale watching in <a href="/wiki/El_Vizca%C3%ADno" class="mw-redirect" title="El Vizca\xc3\xadno">El Vizca\xc3\xadno</a>, with people trying to enter in contact with the animal. This practice is not recommended by most whale watchers</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In Uruguay, where whales can be watched from the beach, legislators have designated the country\'s territorial waters as a sanctuary for whales and dolphins.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It is illegal to be less than 300 metres from a whale.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Locations">Locations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Locations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Whale watching tours are available in various locations and climates. By area, they are:\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Atlantic_and_Indian_oceans">Atlantic and Indian oceans</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Atlantic and Indian oceans"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="South_Africa">South Africa</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: South Africa"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Brydes_whale.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Brydes_whale.jpg/220px-Brydes_whale.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Brydes_whale.jpg/330px-Brydes_whale.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Brydes_whale.jpg/440px-Brydes_whale.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2294" data-file-height="1355" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Brydes_whale" class="mw-redirect" title="Brydes whale">Brydes whale</a> in <a href="/wiki/False_Bay" title="False Bay">False Bay</a>, South Africa</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, the town of <a href="/wiki/Hermanus" title="Hermanus">Hermanus</a> is one of the world centers for whale watching. Between May and December <a href="/wiki/Southern_right_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern right whales">southern right whales</a> come so close to the Cape shoreline that visitors can watch whales from their hotels. The town employs a "whale crier" (cf <a href="/wiki/Town_crier" title="Town crier">town crier</a>) to walk through the town announcing where whales have been seen.\n</p><p>You can watch the whales in Hermanus from the cliff tops, from a boat or the air. Boat-based whale watching tours are available out of the Hermanus New harbour which allows the public to view southern right whales from June till Mid December. <a href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Elizabeth">Port Elizabeth</a> runs a boat-based whale watching tour out of the Port Elizabeth harbour which allows the public to view southern right whales from July to November, humpback whales from June to August and November to January, and Bryde\'s whales all year round, up-close. Visitors can also see humpback whales from the lighthouse at Cape Recife (the Westerly point of <a href="/wiki/Algoa_Bay" title="Algoa Bay">Algoa Bay</a>), and southern right whales from viewing points along the coast. Boat-based whale watching (and dolphin watching) is also a popular tourist attraction in a number of other coastal towns in South Africa, such as Plettenberg Bay, where the industry is linked to <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation</a> and education efforts through Plettenberg Bay-based volunteer <a href="/wiki/Marine_conservation" title="Marine conservation">marine conservation</a> organisations. <a href="/wiki/Plettenberg_Bay" title="Plettenberg Bay">Plettenberg Bay</a> is visited by southern right whales in the winter months and <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> in the summer months. Bryde\'s whales are resident throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The other famous centre for whale watching is False Bay. Tours leave Gordon\'s Bay and follow the coast around the bay. Species include southern right whales, humpback whales and Bryde\'s whales. Orcas are present during the winter months. Visitors include pilot whales and pygmy sperm whales. Many species of dolphin are encountered including <a href="/wiki/Heaviside%27s_dolphin" title="Heaviside&#39;s dolphin">Heaviside\'s dolphins</a>. The same tours include great white sharks at Seal Island and the African Penguin Colony at Simon\'s Town.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Southwest_Atlantic_\xe2\x80\x93_Argentina,_Brazil_and_Uruguay"><span id="Southwest_Atlantic_.E2.80.93_Argentina.2C_Brazil_and_Uruguay"></span>Southwest Atlantic \xe2\x80\x93 Argentina, Brazil and Uruguay</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Southwest Atlantic \xe2\x80\x93 Argentina, Brazil and Uruguay"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg/220px-Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg/330px-Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg/440px-Baleia_de_Bryde.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="856" /></a><figcaption> <a href="/wiki/Brydes_whale" class="mw-redirect" title="Brydes whale">Brydes whale</a> breaching in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Baia_de_Castelhanos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Baia de Castelhanos (page does not exist)">Baia de Castelhanos</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Sao_Paulo" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Paulo">Sao Paulo</a>, Brazil</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, humpbacks are observed off <a href="/wiki/Salvador,_Bahia" title="Salvador, Bahia">Salvador</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bahia_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahia State">Bahia State</a> and at the National Marine Park of <a href="/wiki/Abrolhos_Marine_National_Park" title="Abrolhos Marine National Park">Abrolhos</a> during their breeding season in austral winter and spring. Likewise, southern right whales are observed from shore in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catarina_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Catarina State">Santa Catarina State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Esp\xc3\xadrito Santo">Esp\xc3\xadrito Santo</a> during the same season. Mother/calf pairs can come as close to shore as 30 meters (about 100 feet). Income from whale watching bolsters coastal communities and has made the township of <a href="/wiki/Imbituba" title="Imbituba">Imbituba</a>, the Brazilian "whale capital".\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pen%C3%ADnsula_Vald%C3%A9s" class="mw-redirect" title="Pen\xc3\xadnsula Vald\xc3\xa9s">Pen\xc3\xadnsula Vald\xc3\xa9s</a> in <a href="/wiki/Patagonia" title="Patagonia">Patagonia</a> hosts (in winter) the largest breeding population of southern right whales, with more than 2,000 catalogued by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_Conservation_Institute&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Whale Conservation Institute (page does not exist)">Whale Conservation Institute</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Alliance" title="Ocean Alliance">Ocean Alliance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The region contains six natural reserves, and is considered to be one of the premier whale watching destinations in the world, particularly around the town of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Pir%C3%A1mides" title="Puerto Pir\xc3\xa1mides">Puerto Pir\xc3\xa1mides</a> and the city of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Madryn" title="Puerto Madryn">Puerto Madryn</a>, as the whales come within 200&#160;m (660&#160;ft) of the main beach and play a major part in the large <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> industry in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a>, southern right whales are observable from the beach in two coastal departments \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Maldonado_Department" title="Maldonado Department">Maldonado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rocha_Department" title="Rocha Department">Rocha</a> \xe2\x80\x93 from June to November.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The points where most sightings in Maldonado are made are <a href="/wiki/Punta_Colorada" title="Punta Colorada">Punta Colorada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punta_Negra,_Uruguay" title="Punta Negra, Uruguay">Punta Negra</a>, Playa Mansa and Punta Salinas in <a href="/wiki/Punta_del_Este" title="Punta del Este">Punta del Este</a>, and in Rocha off <a href="/wiki/La_Paloma,_Rocha" title="La Paloma, Rocha">La Paloma</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Pedrera,_Rocha" title="La Pedrera, Rocha">La Pedrera</a> beaches.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Northeast_Atlantic">Northeast Atlantic</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Northeast Atlantic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Tidal straits, inlets, lagoons, and varying water temperatures provide diverse habitats for multiple cetacean species. Substantial numbers live off the coasts of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. Commercial car ferries crossing the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a> from <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> and Ireland to Spain and France often pass by enormous <a href="/wiki/Blue_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue whales">blue whales</a> and much smaller <a href="/wiki/Harbor_porpoise" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbor porpoise">harbor porpoise</a>. Land-based tours can often view these animals.\n</p><p>Off the south coast of Ireland, <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whales</a> are regularly seen on <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching_in_Ireland" title="Whale watching in Ireland">organized whale watching trips</a> between July and February. Species seen all year include <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orca" title="Orca">orcas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harbour_porpoise" title="Harbour porpoise">harbour porpoises</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">common</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Risso%27s_dolphin" title="Risso&#39;s dolphin">Risso\'s dolphins</a>. There is also a resident group of bottlenose dolphins in the <a href="/wiki/Shannon_Estuary" title="Shannon Estuary">Shannon Estuary</a> which attracts tourists all year round.\n<a href="/wiki/Chanonry_Point" title="Chanonry Point">Chanonry Point</a> is one of the best spots in the UK to view <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphins</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The dolphins are visible from the shore, particularly on an incoming tide when they play and fish in the strong currents. Other wildlife, including <a href="/wiki/Porpoise" title="Porpoise">porpoises</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey seals</a>, can also regularly be spotted.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Northern_Norway" title="Northern Norway">Northern Norway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nordland" title="Nordland">Nordland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Troms" title="Troms">Troms</a> counties) orcas are visible in the <a href="/wiki/Vestfjorden_(Norway)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vestfjorden (Norway)">Vestfjorden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tysfjorden" title="Tysfjorden">Tysfjorden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ofotfjorden" class="mw-redirect" title="Ofotfjorden">Ofotfjorden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andfjorden" title="Andfjorden">Andfjorden</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Herring" title="Herring">herring</a> gathers in the <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjords</a> to stay over the winter and off the <a href="/wiki/Lofoten_islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Lofoten islands">Lofoten islands</a> during the summer. At <a href="/wiki/Andenes" title="Andenes">Andenes</a> on <a href="/wiki/And%C3%B8ya" title="And\xc3\xb8ya">And\xc3\xb8ya</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vester%C3%A5len" title="Vester\xc3\xa5len">Vester\xc3\xa5len</a> and around <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%B8tt%C3%B8ya" title="Kr\xc3\xb8tt\xc3\xb8ya">Kr\xc3\xb8tt\xc3\xb8ya</a> in Troms, <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whales</a> can be observed year round, summer whale watching trips occur from May till September, winter trips with killer whales and humpback whales are offered from October till April. <a href="/wiki/Troms%C3%B8_(city)" title="Troms\xc3\xb8 (city)">Troms\xc3\xb8</a> also offers whale watching for sperm and other whales. The continental shelf <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eggakanten&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eggakanten (page does not exist)">Eggakanten</a> and deep water where the sperm whales congregate, is very close to shore, beginning only 7,000 meters (23,000&#160;ft) from the Andenes harbour.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> whale watching is available in the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a>. <a href="/wiki/Lagos,_Portugal" title="Lagos, Portugal">Lagos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portim%C3%A3o" title="Portim\xc3\xa3o">Portim\xc3\xa3o</a> are the most important whale-watching places. The species observed in this area are the fin, killer, and <a href="/wiki/Pilot_whale" title="Pilot whale">pilot whale</a>, and the bottlenose, common, and <a href="/wiki/Striped_dolphin" title="Striped dolphin">striped dolphin</a>.\n</p><p>In the middle of the Northeast Atlantic, around the <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a> archipelagos, whale watching is on the increase and popular due to more protection and education. One of the most common whales in these regions is the sperm whale, especially groups of calving females.\n</p><p>In Spain whale watching is available along the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">Canary Islands</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tarifa" title="Tarifa">Tarifa</a> is the most important whale watching town in the Strait of Gibraltar; this gateway to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> is also a central point in between the colder waters to the North and the tropical waters off of Africa: a good route for migrating cetaceans. The species observed in this area are the bottlenose, common, and striped dolphin, and the pilot, sperm, fin, and killer whale.\nIn the Canary Islands it is possible to see these and others, such as the blue, <a href="/wiki/Beaked_whale" title="Beaked whale">beaked</a>, <a href="/wiki/False_killer_whale" title="False killer whale">false killer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bryde%27s_whale" title="Bryde&#39;s whale">Bryde\'s whale</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_spotted_dolphin" title="Atlantic spotted dolphin">Atlantic spotted</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rough-toothed_dolphin" title="Rough-toothed dolphin">rough-toothed</a>, and Risso\'s dolphin.\n</p><p>In Iceland it is possible to see whales in <a href="/wiki/Eyjafj%C3%B6r%C3%B0ur" title="Eyjafj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur">Eyjafj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brei%C3%B0afj%C3%B6r%C3%B0ur" title="Brei\xc3\xb0afj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur">Brei\xc3\xb0afj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skj%C3%A1lfandi" title="Skj\xc3\xa1lfandi">Skj\xc3\xa1lfandi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faxafl%C3%B3i" title="Faxafl\xc3\xb3i">Faxafl\xc3\xb3i</a>. The towns offering whale watching are <a href="/wiki/Dalv%C3%ADk" title="Dalv\xc3\xadk">Dalv\xc3\xadk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hauganes" title="Hauganes">Hauganes</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BAsav%C3%ADk" title="H\xc3\xbasav\xc3\xadk">H\xc3\xbasav\xc3\xadk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akureyri" title="Akureyri">Akureyri</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%B3lmav%C3%ADk" title="H\xc3\xb3lmav\xc3\xadk">H\xc3\xb3lmav\xc3\xadk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grundarfj%C3%B6r%C3%B0ur" title="Grundarfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur">Grundarfj\xc3\xb6r\xc3\xb0ur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a>. Most common are the <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke</a>, humpback, blue, killer, and sperm whale, as well as the <a href="/wiki/White-beaked_dolphin" title="White-beaked dolphin">white-beaked dolphin</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Harbour_porpoise" title="Harbour porpoise">harbour porpoise</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Northwest_Atlantic">Northwest Atlantic</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Northwest Atlantic"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Photo of whale with head in the air and two-thirds of its body out of the water, falling onto its back" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg/220px-Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg/330px-Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg/440px-Humpback_stellwagen_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3094" data-file-height="1753" /></a><figcaption>A humpback breaching in the <a href="/wiki/Stellwagen_Bank_National_Marine_Sanctuary" title="Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary">Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary</a>. This is a behavior commonly seen in the area.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">New England</a> and off the east coast of <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> in the United States, the whale watching season typically takes place from about mid-spring through October, depending both on weather and precise location. It is here that the <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whale</a>, and the very endangered/heavily protected <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">North Atlantic right whale</a> are often observed. For generations, areas like the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Maine" title="Gulf of Maine">Gulf of Maine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stellwagen_Bank_National_Marine_Sanctuary" title="Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary">Stellwagen Bank National Marine Sanctuary</a> (part of the inner waters formed by <a href="/wiki/Cape_Cod" title="Cape Cod">Cape Cod</a>\'s hooked shape) have been important feeding grounds for these species: to this day a very large portion of the waters off the Eastern Seaboard are rich in <a href="/wiki/Sand_lance" title="Sand lance">sand lance</a> and other nutritious treats for mothers to teach their calves to feed on.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the past this area was the US whaling industry\'s capital, particularly <a href="/wiki/Nantucket" title="Nantucket">Nantucket</a>, an island just off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">Massachusetts</a>. Though whaling has been banned for many years,  and strict laws prohibit molestation of these large wild mammals, it is not unknown for the whales to approach whale watching boats uninvited, particularly curious calves and juveniles: it is not unknown in particular, for example, for juvenile humpbacks to approach the boat and <a href="/wiki/Spyhop" class="mw-redirect" title="Spyhop">spyhop</a> to get a better look at the humans aboard. In recent years it is also not uncommon to see these animals playing and feeding in harbors, including <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> or <a href="/wiki/Boston" title="Boston">Boston</a> where fish species of interest to the whales have lately returned in astonishing numbers. As of 2011, an expert from <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a> has recorded the vocalizations of six whale species including the humpback, the fin whale, and the massive <a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">blue whale</a> within close proximity of the <a href="/wiki/Verrazano-Narrows_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Verrazano-Narrows Bridge">Verrazano-Narrows Bridge</a> in the lower portion of <a href="/wiki/New_York_Harbor" title="New York Harbor">New York Harbor</a> and there is at least one company offering marine life tours out of The <a href="/wiki/Rockaway_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Rockaway Peninsula">Rockaway Peninsula</a> in Queens.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Httpwwwnydailynewscomny_local_whales_return_to_new_york_city_massive_mammals_appearing_again_in_seas_near_cityhtml_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Httpwwwnydailynewscomny_local_whales_return_to_new_york_city_massive_mammals_appearing_again_in_seas_near_cityhtml-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Due to these increasingly frequent visits, new laws address the safety of boaters, commercial fishermen, and the whales themselves: off the coast of Boston, for example, cargo vessels must slow down to protect the much slower <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">North Atlantic right whale</a> and there is talk of erecting an apparatus for the much more heavily trafficked waters surrounding New York City that can warn boats of a whale\'s presence and location so as to avoid accidentally striking the animal.<sup id="cite_ref-Httpwwwnydailynewscomny_local_whales_return_to_new_york_city_massive_mammals_appearing_again_in_seas_near_cityhtml_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Httpwwwnydailynewscomny_local_whales_return_to_new_york_city_massive_mammals_appearing_again_in_seas_near_cityhtml-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Because of the relative diversity of whales and dolphins within easy access of shore, cetacean research takes place at <a href="/wiki/Woods_Hole_Oceanographic_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Woods Hole Oceanographic Institute">Woods Hole Oceanographic Institute</a>, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Riverhead_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Riverhead Foundation (page does not exist)">Riverhead Foundation</a> among other centers.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg/220px-Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg/330px-Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg/440px-Whale_watching_Tadoussac_11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2877" data-file-height="1918" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Estuary_of_St._Lawrence" title="Estuary of St. Lawrence">Estuary of  St. Lawrence River</a>, whale watching near <a href="/wiki/Tadoussac" title="Tadoussac">Tadoussac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Eastern <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> has many whale watching tours in the <a href="/wiki/Estuary_of_St._Lawrence" title="Estuary of St. Lawrence">estuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_St._Lawrence#Marine_mammals" title="Gulf of St. Lawrence">gulf</a> of <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Laurence River</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland and Labrador</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a> or <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>. Twenty-two species of whales and dolphins frequent the waters of Newfoundland and Labrador, although the most common are the humpback, minke, fin, Beluga and killer whales. Another popular whale-watching area is at Tadoussac, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, where Belugas favor the extreme depth and admixture of cold fresh water from the <a href="/wiki/Saguenay_River" title="Saguenay River">Saguenay River</a> into the inland end of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_St._Lawrence" title="Gulf of St. Lawrence">Gulf of St. Lawrence</a>. Humpbacks, minkes, fin and blue whales are also frequently seen off Tadoussac. The <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> is an equally important feeding ground for large baleen whales and dozens of other creatures of the sea; it shares a population of migrating humpbacks with America and is a known summer nursery for mother right whales with calves.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On the east coast of the United States, Virginia Beach, Virginia whale watching is a winter activity from the end of December until the middle of March. Fin, humpback, and right whales are seen off the Virginia Beach coast on whale watching boat trips run by the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Aquarium" title="Virginia Aquarium">Virginia Aquarium</a> and Marine Science Center.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Sightings are mostly of juveniles who stay near the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_Bay" title="Chesapeake Bay">Chesapeake Bay</a> where food is plentiful, while the adults continue to the Caribbean to mate. "Mom" and "Dad" pick up their offspring on the way back north where the whole family summers.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg/220px-2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg/330px-2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg/440px-2017_Sarasota_Adventure_Kayak_Guided_Tour_Cormorant_among_the_Fleet_04_FRD_9405.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3853" data-file-height="2065" /></a><figcaption>Ecotour guide stands on a kayak spotting <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">manatees</a>, around <a href="/wiki/Lido_Key" title="Lido Key">Lido Key</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>Ecotourism based on kayak trips is gaining in popularity in warm-water vacation destinations such as <a href="/wiki/Sarasota,_Florida" title="Sarasota, Florida">Sarasota Keys</a>. Guided kayak trips take kayakers on a tour of the local ecosystem. Kayakers can watch dolphins breach and manatees eat sea grass, in shallow bay water.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The waters surrounding Virginia are also a known migration corridor for the endangered <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_right_whale" title="North Atlantic right whale">North Atlantic right whale</a>: Pregnant females must pass through this area around December to reach their birthing grounds down the coast in Georgia and Florida. For these reasons the waters between the <a href="/wiki/Delmarva_Peninsula" title="Delmarva Peninsula">Delmarva Peninsula</a> and the barrier islands that stretch southwards towards northern Florida must be monitored every winter and spring as mothers give birth to their calves, nurse them, and then ready themselves and their younglings to return north for the cooler waters near New England and Canada.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Caribbean">Caribbean</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Caribbean"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>About 25 species are observed in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a>\'s waters, such as humpback whales, sperm whales, beaked whales and many other small cetaceans. Principal whale watching activities are done in <a href="/wiki/Saman%C3%A1_Bay" title="Saman\xc3\xa1 Bay">Saman\xc3\xa1 Bay</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>, a known breeding ground for humpbacks. Caribwhale and the Caribbean Whale Watch Association include operators engaged in sustainable whale watching activity, as well as experts, conservationists and research groups, such as the International Fund for Animal Welfare, Dalhousie University and Association Evasion Tropicale.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Northern_Indian_Ocean">Northern Indian Ocean</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Northern Indian Ocean"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>On the South and East Coasts of <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Maldives" class="mw-redirect" title="The Maldives">The Maldives</a>, the industry is growing. During winter and summer, <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_blue_whale" title="Pygmy blue whale">pygmy blue</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Sperm whales">sperm whales</a> cross the southern tip of the island, migrating to the warmer waters of Southeast Asia.\nMany pygmy blue whales can be seen at Dondra point in Sri Lanka, accessed through the <a href="/wiki/Mirissa" title="Mirissa">Mirissa</a> or <a href="/wiki/Weligama" title="Weligama">Weligama</a> harbour. Whale-watching tours can be arranged in Sri Lanka.\nBlue whales and some types of dolphins can be seen in the sea of <a href="/wiki/Mirissa" title="Mirissa">Mirissa</a> in Sri Lanka. Many sightings have been reported from November to April.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Northern_Mediterranean_Sea">Northern Mediterranean Sea</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Northern Mediterranean Sea"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In the Pelagos Sanctuary for Mediterranean Marine Mammals, located in the waters of Italy, France and Monaco, there are eight species of marine mammals residents, most of them all year.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Frequent summer excursions depart from the ports of Genoa and Imperia, in Liguria, Northern Italy.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Pacific_Ocean">Pacific Ocean</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pacific Ocean"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="East_Pacific_\xe2\x80\x93Colombia,_Ecuador_&amp;_Panama"><span id="East_Pacific_.E2.80.93Colombia.2C_Ecuador_.26_Panama"></span>East Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Colombia, Ecuador &amp; Panama</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: East Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Colombia, Ecuador &amp; Panama"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG/220px-Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG/330px-Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG/440px-Ballena_jorobada_y_ballenato_en_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption>Humpback whale species in <a href="/wiki/Uramba_Bah%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1laga_National_Natural_Park" title="Uramba Bah\xc3\xada M\xc3\xa1laga National Natural Park">Uramba Bah\xc3\xada M\xc3\xa1laga National Natural Park</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, considered the favorite place for whales give birth to their young, making it a tourist destination</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, the towns of <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%ADa_Solano" title="Bah\xc3\xada Solano">Bah\xc3\xada Solano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nuqu%C3%AD" title="Nuqu\xc3\xad">Nuqu\xc3\xad</a> are visited by a large number of Humpback whales from late July to the beginning of October.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In southern Costa Rica, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Marino_Ballena_National_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Marino Ballena National Park (page does not exist)">Marino Ballena National Park</a> has two seasons when whales visit.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Islands" title="Pearl Islands">Pearl Islands</a> archipelago receive an estimated 300 humpbacks whale from late June to late November. These had become now the main attraction for whale watching tours starting in <a href="/wiki/Panama_City" title="Panama City">Panama City</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Chiriqui" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf of Chiriqui">Gulf of Chiriqui</a>, the World Heritage Site of <a href="/wiki/Coiba_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Coiba Island">Coiba Island</a> National Park and the islands near the town of Boca Chica are offering opportunities for whale watching. Isla Iguana near <a href="/wiki/Pedas%C3%AD_township,_Los_Santos" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedas\xc3\xad township, Los Santos">Pedasi</a> is now a popular destination for whale watchers. Several foundations train local community members to perform as guide and captains for whale watching tours.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, from June to September, there are many sites from which large groups of humpback whales can be seen, including Isla de la Plata (AKA Little Galapagos) and <a href="/wiki/Salinas,_Ecuador" title="Salinas, Ecuador">Salinas</a>, at the tip of the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Elena_Peninsula" title="Santa Elena Peninsula">Santa Elena Peninsula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Northeast_Pacific_\xe2\x80\x93Mexico_and_United_States"><span id="Northeast_Pacific_.E2.80.93Mexico_and_United_States"></span>Northeast Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Mexico and United States</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Northeast Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Mexico and United States"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Watching_Orcas_(Monterey,_2007).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Watching_Orcas_%28Monterey%2C_2007%29.jpg/220px-Watching_Orcas_%28Monterey%2C_2007%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Watching_Orcas_%28Monterey%2C_2007%29.jpg/330px-Watching_Orcas_%28Monterey%2C_2007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Watching_Orcas_%28Monterey%2C_2007%29.jpg/440px-Watching_Orcas_%28Monterey%2C_2007%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2720" data-file-height="1293" /></a><figcaption>Watching <a href="/wiki/Orca" title="Orca">orcas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Bay" title="Monterey Bay">Monterey Bay</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_(Megaptera_novaeangliae),_Juneau,_Alaska,_Estados_Unidos,_2017-08-17,_DD_19.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_%28Megaptera_novaeangliae%29%2C_Juneau%2C_Alaska%2C_Estados_Unidos%2C_2017-08-17%2C_DD_19.jpg/220px-Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_%28Megaptera_novaeangliae%29%2C_Juneau%2C_Alaska%2C_Estados_Unidos%2C_2017-08-17%2C_DD_19.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_%28Megaptera_novaeangliae%29%2C_Juneau%2C_Alaska%2C_Estados_Unidos%2C_2017-08-17%2C_DD_19.jpg/330px-Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_%28Megaptera_novaeangliae%29%2C_Juneau%2C_Alaska%2C_Estados_Unidos%2C_2017-08-17%2C_DD_19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_%28Megaptera_novaeangliae%29%2C_Juneau%2C_Alaska%2C_Estados_Unidos%2C_2017-08-17%2C_DD_19.jpg/440px-Avistamiento_de_ballenas_jorabadas_%28Megaptera_novaeangliae%29%2C_Juneau%2C_Alaska%2C_Estados_Unidos%2C_2017-08-17%2C_DD_19.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4054" data-file-height="1986" /></a><figcaption>Humpback whales watching (<i>Megaptera novaeangliae</i>), Juneau, Alaska, United States.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>On the West Coast of Canada and the United States, excellent whale watching can be found in Alaska (summer), British Columbia, and the San Juan Islands/Puget Sound in <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, where whales are \nsighted from shore nearly every day, year-round.<sup id="cite_ref-OrcaNetwork_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OrcaNetwork-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Three types of orca pods can be observed in the Northeast Pacific: resident, transient, and offshore killer whales.<sup id="cite_ref-OrcaNetwork_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OrcaNetwork-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Coast" title="Oregon Coast">Oregon Coast</a>, several whale species, especially <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">gray whales</a>, may be seen year-round, and the state trains volunteers to assist tourists in the winter months, during whale migration season.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, good whale-watching can be found year-round on the Southern California coast. During the winter and spring (December\xe2\x80\x93May), <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">gray whales</a> can be seen from shore on their annual migration (the best spot being <a href="/wiki/Point_Vicente_Light" class="mw-redirect" title="Point Vicente Light">Point Vicente</a>), while <a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">blue whales</a> are often seen between July and October. <a href="/wiki/Fin_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Fin whales">Fin whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minke_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Minke whales">minke whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orcas" class="mw-redirect" title="Orcas">orcas</a>, and various species of dolphins can be seen year-round.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In spring, summer, and fall at the <a href="/wiki/Farallon_Islands" title="Farallon Islands">Farallon Islands</a> off <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, one may see <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpbacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gray_whale" title="Gray whale">grays</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Blue_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue whales">blue whales</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, the various <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">lagoons</a> of <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Sur" title="Baja California Sur">Baja California Sur</a> become breeding habitat for gray whales in February and March.<sup id="cite_ref-moon_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-moon-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sust_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sust-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nHumpback whales can be seen off the southern tip of Baja California,<sup id="cite_ref-os_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and off Puerto Vallarta in Jalisco on the west coast of Mexico,<sup id="cite_ref-sor_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sor-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Barra de Potosi on the south coast of Mexico in the state of Guerrero.<sup id="cite_ref-paters_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paters-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A number of towns in Mexico celebrate the whale\'s arrival with festivals such as <a href="/wiki/Guerrero_Negro" title="Guerrero Negro">Guerrero Negro</a>, in the first half of February and the port of <a href="/wiki/San_Blas,_Baja_California_Sur" title="San Blas, Baja California Sur">San Blas</a> on 24 and 25 February.<sup id="cite_ref-MexDesOax_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MexDesOax-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In late March 2021, a 70-foot (21&#160;m) blue whale was spotted near the Orange County, California coastline. These mammals are typically seen in summer months, but this blue whale was spotted out of season, heading north, close to the Balboa Pier and Newport Beach shoreline.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Central_Pacific_\xe2\x80\x93Hawaii"><span id="Central_Pacific_.E2.80.93Hawaii"></span>Central Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Hawaii</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Central Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Hawaii"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Each winter 4,000 to 10,000 North Pacific humpback whales migrate from <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> to <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>. In the vast waters that line Alaska\'s coast, an encounter with a whale is likely. In the summer, after thousands of whales have made their way to the rich feeding grounds of Alaska waters, sightings are extremely common.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Whale watching is possible within as well as outside the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands_Humpback_Whale_National_Marine_Sanctuary" title="Hawaiian Islands Humpback Whale National Marine Sanctuary">Hawaiian Islands Humpback Whale National Marine Sanctuary</a>. The best places to see whales in Hawai\xca\xbbi is in the protected channels between the Hawai\xca\xbbian islands. The best months to see the whales here are January and February when you can expect to see between 2 and 4 whales per 15 minute period,<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> although fluctuations between 0 and 20 sightings are normal.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="West_Pacific_\xe2\x80\x93East_and_Southeast_Asia"><span id="West_Pacific_.E2.80.93East_and_Southeast_Asia"></span>West Pacific \xe2\x80\x93East and Southeast Asia</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: West Pacific \xe2\x80\x93East and Southeast Asia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_the_Philippines" title="Whaling in the Philippines">Whaling in the Philippines</a></div>\n<p>Many countries in Asia have large whale watching industries. In 2008 the largest, in terms of number of tourists, were mainland China, Taiwan and Japan. India, Cambodia, Hong Kong, Indonesia, the Philippines and the Maldives also have dolphin watching and some whale watching. China\'s dolphin watching is almost entirely focussed on Sanniang Bay in <a href="/wiki/Guangxi" title="Guangxi">Guangxi</a>. Taiwan has several whale watching ports on its east coast. Japan has a range of whale and dolphin watching businesses on all main islands and <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Island" title="Okinawa Island">Okinawa</a>, Zamami, Ogasawara, Mikura-Jima and Miyake-jima.<sup id="cite_ref-OConnor2009_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OConnor2009-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, over thirty species of whales and dolphins can be observed around <a href="/wiki/Pamilacan" title="Pamilacan">Pamilacan</a> in Central <a href="/wiki/Visayas" title="Visayas">Visayas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Davao_Gulf" title="Davao Gulf">Davao Gulf</a>, the northern coast of the province-island <a href="/wiki/Babuyan_Islands" title="Babuyan Islands">Babuyan Islands</a> in <a href="/wiki/Batanes" title="Batanes">Batanes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pasaleng_Bay" title="Pasaleng Bay">Pasaleng Bay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Malampaya_Sound" title="Malampaya Sound">Malampaya Sound</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palawan" title="Palawan">Palawan</a>. The Visayas is particularly known area for dolphin sightings, and is home to one of the larger populations of the <a href="/wiki/Fraser%27s_dolphin" title="Fraser&#39;s dolphin">Fraser\'s dolphin</a> in the world. Dolphin species in the Visayas are attracted to fish lures and to commercial fishing operations. In the northernmost province of Batanes, at least 12 species of whales and dolphins has been sighted, making it the single location in the country with the highest cetacean diversity. There seems to be no specific whale watching season in the Philippines, although the calmer waters of the summer season typically provides the best conditions. Some populations, like those of the <a href="/wiki/Irrawaddy_dolphin" title="Irrawaddy dolphin">Irrawaddy dolphin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryde%27s_whale" title="Bryde&#39;s whale">Bryde\'s whale</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a> in Batanes, appear migratory. Other populations have yet to be studied. Some former coastal whaling communities in the Philippines have also started to generate whale watching income.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Southeast_Pacific_\xe2\x80\x93Chile_and_Peru"><span id="Southeast_Pacific_.E2.80.93Chile_and_Peru"></span>Southeast Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Chile and Peru</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Southeast Pacific \xe2\x80\x93Chile and Peru"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Corcovado" title="Gulf of Corcovado">Gulf of Corcovado</a> and the waters of <a href="/wiki/Guaitecas_Archipelago" title="Guaitecas Archipelago">Guaitecas Archipelago</a> a variety of whales and dolphins can be been spotted, including: <a href="/wiki/Peale%27s_dolphin" title="Peale&#39;s dolphin">Peale\'s dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chilean_dolphin" title="Chilean dolphin">black dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bottlenose_dolphin" title="Bottlenose dolphin">bottlenose dolphins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whales</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whales</a> and <a href="/wiki/Killer_whale" class="mw-redirect" title="Killer whale">killer whales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Pacificnew2011_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pacificnew2011-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Gulf of Corcovado is "arguably the largest feeding and nursing ground for <a href="/wiki/Blue_whales" class="mw-redirect" title="Blue whales">blue whales</a> [...] in the entire Southern Hemisphere".<sup id="cite_ref-Pacificnew2011_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pacificnew2011-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> All of this makes Guaitecas Archipelago a privilidged place for whale watching.<sup id="cite_ref-Pacificnew2011_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pacificnew2011-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the localities of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Pi%C3%B1ihuil&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pi\xc3\xb1ihuil (page does not exist)">Pi\xc3\xb1ihuil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quell%C3%B3n" title="Quell\xc3\xb3n">Quell\xc3\xb3n</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melinka" title="Melinka">Melinka</a> local fishermen offer whale watching tours.<sup id="cite_ref-Pacificnew2011_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pacificnew2011-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Southwest_Pacific_\xe2\x80\x93_New_Zealand_and_Australia"><span id="Southwest_Pacific_.E2.80.93_New_Zealand_and_Australia"></span>Southwest Pacific \xe2\x80\x93 New Zealand and Australia</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Southwest Pacific \xe2\x80\x93 New Zealand and Australia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg/220px-2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg/330px-2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg/440px-2000-12_Whale_Watching.jpg 2x" data-file-width="923" data-file-height="650" /></a><figcaption>Whale watching in Kaikoura, December 2000</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Photo of whales at surface with buildings in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG/220px-Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG/330px-Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG/440px-Whale_watching_gold_coast.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1977" data-file-height="1230" /></a><figcaption>A couple of humpback whales spotted off the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast, Queensland</a></figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching_in_Australia" title="Whale watching in Australia">Whale watching in Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whale_watching_in_New_Zealand" title="Whale watching in New Zealand">Whale watching in New Zealand</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Kaik%C5%8Dura" title="Kaik\xc5\x8dura">Kaik\xc5\x8dura</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> is a world-famous whale-watching site. The sea around Kaik\xc5\x8dura supports an abundance of sea life, with the town\'s income stemming largely from the tourism generated from whale watching and swimming with or around dolphins. Recently the <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whale</a> watching at Kaik\xc5\x8dura has developed rapidly and now it is an industry leader, arguably the most developed in the world. The town went into recession after the collapse of <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_New_Zealand" title="Whaling in New Zealand">whaling in New Zealand</a>. Its recent development has been used to advocate the benefits of watching whales instead of hunting them.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Coast,_Queensland" title="Sunshine Coast, Queensland">Sunshine Coast</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hervey_Bay" title="Hervey Bay">Hervey Bay</a> (where the whales stay and rest before migrating) in <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> offer reliable whale watching conditions for <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">southern humpback whales</a> from the end of June through to the end of November each year. Whale numbers and activity have increased markedly in recent years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (October 2012)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eden,_New_South_Wales" title="Eden, New South Wales">Eden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Stephens_(New_South_Wales)" title="Port Stephens (New South Wales)">Port Stephens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narooma" class="mw-redirect" title="Narooma">Narooma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byron_Bay,_New_South_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Byron Bay, New South Wales">Byron Bay</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> are other popular hot spots for tours from May to November.\n</p><p>Southern right whales are seen June\xe2\x80\x93August along the south coast of Australia. They are often readily viewed from the coast around <a href="/wiki/Encounter_Bay" title="Encounter Bay">Encounter Bay</a> near <a href="/wiki/Victor_Harbor,_South_Australia" title="Victor Harbor, South Australia">Victor Harbor</a> and up to a hundred at a time may be seen from the cliff tops at the head of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Australian_Bight" title="Great Australian Bight">Great Australian Bight</a> near <a href="/wiki/Yalata,_South_Australia" title="Yalata, South Australia">Yalata</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Australia" title="Whaling in Australia">Whaling in Australia</a>.\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Right_Whale_(Eubalaena_australis)_(16358018502).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Southern_Right_Whale_%28Eubalaena_australis%29_%2816358018502%29.jpg/220px-Southern_Right_Whale_%28Eubalaena_australis%29_%2816358018502%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Southern_Right_Whale_%28Eubalaena_australis%29_%2816358018502%29.jpg/330px-Southern_Right_Whale_%28Eubalaena_australis%29_%2816358018502%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Southern_Right_Whale_%28Eubalaena_australis%29_%2816358018502%29.jpg/440px-Southern_Right_Whale_%28Eubalaena_australis%29_%2816358018502%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="567" /></a><figcaption>Southern right whale, offshore from Cheynes, <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> </figcaption></figure>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>, whales are watched near <a href="/wiki/Cape_Naturaliste" title="Cape Naturaliste">Cape Naturaliste</a> in the south-east <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Cape_Leeuwin" title="Cape Leeuwin">Cape Leeuwin</a> where the Indian and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern</a> Oceans meet.\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a> there are many spots to see whales, both from land or aboard ship. Albany on the south coast of Western Australia the town where the last land based whaling station in the southern hemisphere was located is now home to a thriving whale watching industry.
