In <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> a popular site is Logan\'s Beach at <a href="/wiki/Warrnambool,_Victoria" class="mw-redirect" title="Warrnambool, Victoria">Warrnambool</a>, as well as in the waters off <a href="/wiki/Port_Fairy,_Victoria" class="mw-redirect" title="Port Fairy, Victoria">Port Fairy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Victoria" title="Portland, Victoria">Portland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> whales can be seen all along the east coast and even on the <a href="/wiki/Derwent_River_(Tasmania)" class="mw-redirect" title="Derwent River (Tasmania)">River Derwent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a> whales are watched in the <a href="/wiki/Great_Australian_Bight" title="Great Australian Bight">Great Australian Bight</a> Marine Park areas and closer to Adelaide at <a href="/wiki/Victor_Harbor,_South_Australia" title="Victor Harbor, South Australia">Victor Harbor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In eastern Australia, whale watching occurs in many spots along the Pacific coast. From headlands, whales may often be seen making their migration south. At times, whales even make it into <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Sydney Harbour">Sydney Harbour</a>.\n</p><p>New South Wales National Parks and Wildlife took an active role in 2010 during the peak southern whale watching<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> season between May and November with the launch of its whale watching site.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Whaling_and_whale_watching">Whaling and whale watching</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Whaling and whale watching"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The three biggest <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> nations (<a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a>) have growing whale watching industries. The next four whaling nations (<a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>) also have whale watching industries. Indeed, Iceland had the fastest-growing whale watching industry in the world between 1994 and 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Canada">Canada</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Canada"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Canada" title="Whaling in Canada">Whaling in Canada</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg/220px-Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg/330px-Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg/440px-Whale_watching_in_St._Andrews.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a><figcaption>Whale watching business in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Andrews,_New_Brunswick" title="Saint Andrews, New Brunswick">Saint Andrews, New Brunswick</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Whale watching and hunting take place in different regions of Canada: the former mainly on Atlantic and Pacific coasts, the latter exclusively in the Arctic. Whale watching happens in the Saint Lawrence River, western Hudson\'s Bay near Churchill, and British Columbia. Hunting takes place in eastern Hudson\'s Bay (Nunavik, Quebec), Nunavut and the Beaufort Sea. Researchers have suggested the hunting areas would benefit more from whale watching than hunting since hunting takes more resources than it earns.<sup id="cite_ref-hoover_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hoover-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2018, \nCanada implemented new restrictions intended to cut human interactions with whales. Following these rules, all boats must stay farther away from the mammals than before. Some activities, including snorkeling with humpbacks, are banned.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Greenland">Greenland</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Greenland"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Greenland" class="mw-redirect" title="Whaling in Greenland">Whaling in Greenland</a></div>\n<p>Greenland has small whale watching operations in Disko Bay<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Nuuk.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Both areas have beluga hunts.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There has been controversy over who is allowed to participate in hunts and consume the meat.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Norway">Norway</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Norway"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Norway" title="Whaling in Norway">Whaling in Norway</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg/220px-Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="100" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg/330px-Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg/440px-Tysfjord_orca_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1054" data-file-height="481" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Orca" title="Orca">Orca</a> near <a href="/wiki/Tysfjorden" title="Tysfjorden">Tysfjorden</a>, Norway</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Enjoyment of observing live cetaceans is rather separated from the domestic whaling industry in Norway; however, whale watching has become a popular national tourist attraction in recent years, especially in <a href="/wiki/Andfjorden" title="Andfjorden">Andfjorden</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vester%C3%A5len" title="Vester\xc3\xa5len">Vester\xc3\xa5len</a> and <a href="/wiki/Troms" title="Troms">Troms</a>) and around <a href="/wiki/Troms%C3%B8_Municipality" class="mw-redirect" title="Troms\xc3\xb8 Municipality">Troms\xc3\xb8</a>.\n</p>\n<ul><li>Uniquely, public opinions against whaling showed sudden rises in 2014, when a possibly pregnant <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whale</a> <i>Heiko</i>, named after <a href="/wiki/Keiko_(orca)" title="Keiko (orca)">Keiko</a> the <a href="/wiki/Orca" title="Orca">orca</a> and a local cetacean researcher Heike Vester who monitors the whale\'s safety, successfully shook off whaling vessels by taking refuge in the very shallow fjord of <a href="/wiki/Lofoten" title="Lofoten">Lofoten</a>, where large whales had not been seen for years; this has provided chances for locals to witness cetaceans at close range. Heiko\'s appearance soon resulted in an increase in interest among locals.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As time passed, Heiko attracted more domestic and international interest, which has resulted in greater questioning and opposition to the whaling industry in Norway.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Japan">Japan</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Japan"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Japan" title="Whaling in Japan">Whaling in Japan</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Illustration_of_Whale_1,_Edo_period,_18th-19th_century,_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Illustration_of_Whale_1%2C_Edo_period%2C_18th-19th_century%2C_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG/220px-Illustration_of_Whale_1%2C_Edo_period%2C_18th-19th_century%2C_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Illustration_of_Whale_1%2C_Edo_period%2C_18th-19th_century%2C_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG/330px-Illustration_of_Whale_1%2C_Edo_period%2C_18th-19th_century%2C_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Illustration_of_Whale_1%2C_Edo_period%2C_18th-19th_century%2C_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG/440px-Illustration_of_Whale_1%2C_Edo_period%2C_18th-19th_century%2C_color_on_paper_-_Tokyo_National_Museum_-_DSC05512.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5201" data-file-height="2869" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">Humpback whale</a> illustration from the <a href="/wiki/Edo_period" title="Edo period">Edo period</a>, 18th-19th century</figcaption></figure>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg/220px-2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg/330px-2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg/440px-2006%E5%B9%B45%E6%9C%888%E6%97%A5_%E5%BE%A1%E8%94%B5%E5%B3%B6%E3%83%84%E3%82%A2%E3%83%BC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="576" /></a><figcaption>Resident <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pacific_bottlenose_dolphin" title="Indo-Pacific bottlenose dolphin">Indo-Pacific bottlenose dolphins</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mikura-jima" title="Mikura-jima">Mikura-jima</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Erich_Hoyt" title="Erich Hoyt">Erich Hoyt</a> and other conservationists argue that a whale is worth more alive and watched than dead.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The goal is to persuade their governments to curtail whaling activities. This debate continues at the <a href="/wiki/International_Whaling_Commission" title="International Whaling Commission">International Whaling Commission</a>, particularly since whaling countries complain that the scarcity of <a href="/wiki/Whale_meat" title="Whale meat">whale meat</a> and other products has increased their value. However, the whale meat market has collapsed, and in Japan the government subsidizes the market through distribution in schools and other promotion. In 1997, 2,000 tonnes of whale meat were sold for $30m \xe2\x80\x93 a 10-tonne <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whale</a> would thus have been worth $150,000. There is no agreement as to how to value a single animal although its true value is probably much higher. However, it is clear from most coastal communities that are involved in whale watching that profits can be made and are more horizontally distributed throughout the community than if the animals were killed by the whaling industry.<sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2009_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2009-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157_5-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyt,_E_2001._pp._1-157-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>There have been disputes and skirmishes between whale watching operators and whalers in the nation. For example, whaling was operated right in front of watching vessels, causing malaise among domestic and international passengers on board, and domestic disputes spread on the Internet in <a href="/wiki/Nemuro_Strait" title="Nemuro Strait">Nemuro Strait</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Local tour operators confirmed that targeted species for hunting such as Baird\'s beaked whales and <a href="/wiki/Dall%27s_porpoise" title="Dall&#39;s porpoise">Dall\'s porpoises</a> are known to disappear or have become harder to approach in the seasons of whaling operations in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Recent notable declines and disappearances (or abandoning of historical habitats) of <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Baird%27s_beaked_whale" title="Baird&#39;s beaked whale">Baird\'s beaked whales</a> in coastal waters caused by commercial and scientific whaling that have been operated in wide ranges off the eastern half of <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hokkaido" title="Hokkaido">Hokkaido</a> especially off <a href="/wiki/Abashiri" title="Abashiri">Abashiri</a>, Gulf of <a href="/wiki/Sendai" title="Sendai">Sendai</a>, and along the coast of <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">Chiba</a>, caused dramatic decreases in sightings of both species in many areas, enough for whalers to be forced to change their operating ranges, and a watching operator in <a href="/wiki/Muroran" title="Muroran">Muroran</a> claimed that whaling affected the profits of the operator due to serious declines and low rates of successful minke sightings in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Hunting of Baird\'s beaked whales in <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Japan" title="Sea of Japan">Sea of Japan</a> has ceased in recent decades, and the whales have been said to have become more friendly during this period; however, commercial whaling was resumed in Sea of Japan and caused concerns among cetacean conservationists.</li>\n<li>The first whale watching in Japan was conducted in <a href="/wiki/Bonin_Islands" title="Bonin Islands">Bonin Islands</a> in 1998 by a group called "Geisharen <i>\xe9\xaf\xa8\xe8\x80\x85\xe9\x80\xa3</i>" which was formed by groups of domestic and international people including both domestic and international celebrities and notable cetacean researchers and conservationists such as <a href="/wiki/Roger_Payne" title="Roger Payne">Roger Payne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Erich_Hoyt" title="Erich Hoyt">Erich Hoyt</a>, Richard Oliver, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Darling" title="Jim Darling">Jim Darling</a>, John Ford, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kyusoku_Iwamoto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kyusoku Iwamoto (page does not exist)">Kyusoku Iwamoto</a> (cartoonist), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hutoushiki_Ueki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hutoushiki Ueki (page does not exist)">Hutoushiki Ueki</a> (science writer), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nobuyuki_Miyazaki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nobuyuki Miyazaki (page does not exist)">Nobuyuki Miyazaki</a> (head chief of the Atmosphere and Ocean Research Institute of The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nobuaki_Mochizuki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Nobuaki Mochizuki (page does not exist)">Nobuaki Mochizuki</a> (one of the world\'s first whale photographers to record a <a href="/wiki/North_Pacific_right_whale" title="North Pacific right whale">North Pacific right whale</a> underwater in 1990 in Bonin Islands), and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Junko_Sakuma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Junko Sakuma (page does not exist)">Junko Sakuma</a> (freelancer).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> During this time until before the group reach the destination, the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Agriculture,_Forestry_and_Fisheries_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries (Japan)">Ministry of Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries (Japan)</a> and other groups and anonymous individuals watched the group\'s movements and tried to pressure them not to conduct the tour.<sup id="cite_ref-Obara1996_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obara1996-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Prior to this movement, those who claimed conserving marine mammals including <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">pinnipeds</a>, or individuals who tried to correct illegal and over-extensive hunts (including <a href="/wiki/C._W._Nicol" title="C. W. Nicol">C. W. Nicol</a>, who was a sympathizer with Japan\'s whaling industries) or domestic media that have done reporting assignments<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in Japan had been discriminated.<sup id="cite_ref-Obara1996_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Obara1996-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> These include a former fisherman who was ostracized from the community, later to become a whale-watching operator.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Several other tours have been operated by former whalers or dolphin hunters in places such as <a href="/wiki/Abashiri" title="Abashiri">Abashiri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Muroto,_K%C5%8Dchi" title="Muroto, K\xc5\x8dchi">Muroto</a>.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Russia">Russia</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Russia"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Whaling in Russia">Whaling in Russia</a></div>\n<p>Russian whale watching involves orcas off the Kamchatka peninsula on the edge of the Sea of Okhotsk.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\nBeluga are hunted in the Sea of Okhotsk as well as farther north. Erich Hoyt of the Whale and Dolphin Conservation Society has identified other places in Russia to develop whale watching.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Iceland">Iceland</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Iceland"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Whaling_in_Iceland" title="Whaling in Iceland">Whaling in Iceland</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg/220px-BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg/330px-BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg/440px-BlueWhaleWithCalf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2973" data-file-height="1977" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">Blue whale</a> with calf, <a href="/wiki/%C3%93lafsv%C3%ADk" title="\xc3\x93lafsv\xc3\xadk">\xc3\x93lafsv\xc3\xadk</a>, Iceland</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Upon the resumption of whaling in Iceland in August 2003, pro-whaling groups, such as fishermen who argue that increased stocks of whales deplete fish populations, suggested that sustainable whaling and whale watching could live side by side. Whale watching lobbyists, such as <a href="/wiki/H%C3%BAsav%C3%ADk_Whale_Museum" title="H\xc3\xbasav\xc3\xadk Whale Museum">H\xc3\xbasav\xc3\xadk Whale Museum</a> curator Asbjorn Bjorgvinsson, counter that the most inquisitive whales, which approach boats very closely and provide much of the entertainment on whale-watching trips, will be the first to be taken. Pro-whaling organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/High_North_Alliance" title="High North Alliance">High North Alliance</a> on the other hand, claim that some whale-watching companies in Iceland are surviving only because they receive funding from anti-whaling organizations. In 2020, Iceland ceased whaling activities due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> restrictions and decreasing sales to Japan limited the feasibility of a harvest.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> That same year, whaling for minke whales by the only company targeting domestic markets was permanently ended.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A similar decision to halt all whaling activities was made for the summer whaling season of 2021 in light of ongoing pandemic restrictions and steady increases in whale watching tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Portugal">Portugal</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Whale_watching&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Portugal"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_whaling#Twentieth_century" title="History of whaling">History of whaling \xc2\xa7&#160;Twentieth century</a></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg/170px-Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg/255px-Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg/340px-Uma_Baleia_An%C3%A3_nos_A%C3%A7ores..jpg 2x" data-file-width="434" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Balaenoptera_acutorostrata" class="mw-redirect" title="Balaenoptera acutorostrata">Common minke whale</a> <a href="/wiki/Spy_hopping" class="mw-redirect" title="Spy hopping">spy hopping</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>In comparison, the government of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> has promoted an economic policy centred on tourism that includes whale watching. With the decline of whaling in the early 1970s in the islands, many of the communities of the archipelago involved in whaling (including villages and towns, specifically on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Faial_Island" title="Faial Island">Faial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terceira" class="mw-redirect" title="Terceira">Terceira</a>, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island" title="S\xc3\xa3o Miguel Island">S\xc3\xa3o Miguel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pico_Island" title="Pico Island">Pico</a>) were transformed into hubs for whale watching services (that followed the migratory tracts during the summer), while older buildings and factories were re-purposed into museums.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="See_also">See also</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span
